        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer767449737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14514085351732872158"><b>Currently FREE!</b><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://amzn.to/2IuOcQY'>https://amzn.to/2IuOcQY</a><br/><br/>Doe has no memory of her past life. All she knows is that she was found in the trash, bloody and bruised. The cops never tried hard to find out who she really was, thinking that she was just another hooker roughed up by her pimp. Homeless and scared she hooks up with an actual hooker, Nikki. Nikki tells her that her only option of survival is to go to the party Nikki is going to, hook up with one of the bikers there, become their whore, and then she'll be ta</span>
  <span id="freeText14514085351732872158" style="display:none"><b>Currently FREE!</b><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://amzn.to/2IuOcQY">https://amzn.to/2IuOcQY</a><br><br>Doe has no memory of her past life. All she knows is that she was found in the trash, bloody and bruised. The cops never tried hard to find out who she really was, thinking that she was just another hooker roughed up by her pimp. Homeless and scared she hooks up with an actual hooker, Nikki. Nikki tells her that her only option of survival is to go to the party Nikki is going to, hook up with one of the bikers there, become their whore, and then she'll be taken care of. <br><br>Brantley King just got out of prison after serving years for murder. He's a tattoo artist, a drug dealer, and a thief in order to survive. Ever since he was twelve years old it was him and his best friend Preppy. They didn't rely on other people to get what they needed, they made their own way and took what they wanted. Asking no one for help. King hasn't had an easy life and he's a changed man now that he's out of prison. When he first see's Doe at his welcome home party, he doesn't understand the possessiveness he feels, but he wants her, and takes what he wants.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434322770i/15204031.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I. Loved. King! He was possessive and so intense and <b>
  <i>sexy as fuck.</i>
</b> I literally just want to rant about this story and the characters and how much I liked them but I don't want to spoil it for anyone. This story consumed me and once I had started it I did not <i>once</i> get up from my couch until I was finished. WHICH I was so mad about! That stupid cliffhanger :( It killed me and then I just still laid on my couch not knowing what to do because I just wanted <b>more!</b><br><br>Okay, I'm getting off topic here. Anyway, this was such a fucked up story that makes you question why you like this character so much. King was angry, and mean, and he scared Doe at times, so it makes you think you are a little insane to like such a man. But underneath all of that, King cares about people so deeply that you almost can't comprehend it. He doesn't fuck around with the fake smiles, and the small conversations with people he doesn't like. He has those close to him, and everyone else can fuck off, which I actually really liked. It made him more real in a way. <br><br>I don't actually know how to describe how this story effected my emotions. I was angry, and sad, and happy, all through the course of this book. There were dark times that scared me, and made me sad. They were just so deep and emotional that it was captivating. And then you have a character like Preppy who is completely different from King and made me laugh so much and I just sat there with a smile on my face from other times. He was seriously the best secondary character <b>ever.</b> Preppy and King balanced each other and they were fucked up in their own way, and because of that they always had each others back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434324355i/15204210._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It kills me to say this, but I actually didn't like Doe that much. She had a lot of problems, obviously, but it annoyed me some with how she was about her memory. Always saying that she didn't want to do something and ruin <i>her</i> life. As in, the other her, the one in her past who had her memory. At first I got it, but it was just a little annoying that she wouldn't make any decisions that could effect the past <i>her.</i> This is the reason for my 4 star rating, instead of 5.<br><br>Overall, this was still a fantastic story that I am dying to get the rest of. Seriously guys, be prepared for this cliffhanger because I was screaming for more at the end. Literally yelled at my Kindle because I didn't want it to be over.<br><br>I think I fell a little bit in love with T.M Frazier after I read <i>The Dark Light of Day</i> and this book just proved my love. I really don't know how someone can create such amazing books that are so deep, and passionate and just so beautiful it makes you weep. I love this author, I love these books, I just <b>
  <i>love it all.</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434324686ra/15204304.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>ARC kindly provided by the author in exchange for a honest review.</i><br>(Teasers taken from authors Facebook page.)</span>

Doe is th</span>
  <span id="freeText12028890151326926954" style="display:none">★★★★ <b>4.5 Stars</b> ★★★★<br><br><b>Now LIVE!<br>Amazon US: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1ALhF4i">http://amzn.to/1ALhF4i</a><br>Amazon UK: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1AOJb0q">http://amzn.to/1AOJb0q</a></b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434203753i/15182649._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is a spoiler free review, so I am not going to rehash the story for you but I am going to tell you about the amazing and awesome people in this story that I am still thinking about days later. I love flawed and complex characters, especially when they are dark and dangerous and you know that deep down there is a beautiful heart inside that stone exterior that is just bursting to come out. Doe is the girl that brings 3 men alive again in different ways.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434203753i/15182650._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Doe is a missing person, she was found in an alley, bloodied and with no memory. She was thrown into foster care but has recently left to live on the streets. It is now when she is at her lowest that she meets King, Preppy &amp; Bear. Once the initial fear of these intimidating men wears off, she feels confusingly safe when she finds herself captive in King's lair and becomes the woman who will peel back the layers of Brantley King.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434203753i/15182651._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>King is fresh out of prison, he is a tattoo artist by night and an outlaw criminal by day. He is a beautifully intense anti-hero and is drawn to the blond haired, petite feisty female who was trying to sell her soul to the devil in exchange for protection and food.<br><br>Preppy is King's best friend and business partner, they have known each other since King rescued Preppy from his childhood bullies and they are the only family each other have. Preppy has a penchant for bow ties and murder, and he takes it upon himself to become Doe's new friend and big brother.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434203753i/15182652._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bear is the VP of the Beach Bastards MC and has been hanging around with King &amp; Preppy since they were fifteen, he is willing to take Doe as his old lady if King doesn't claim her, and he is as protective as he is fierce. He has always wanted King and Preppy to join him and his MC brothers but is content with working closely with them in mutually beneficial business deals and he always has their back.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434203753i/15182653._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the mystery behind both Doe and King, Doe is struggling to move forward with her life knowing that she has left one behind that she can't remember and King is also hiding the initial reason that he decided he wanted to keep Doe, he needs her for something, and that something happens to be very important to him.<br><br>This book had me turning the pages, it was suspenseful and you absolutely did not see the twists coming. It was dark, but also sweet, funny, angsty and heartbreaking all at the same time. The cliffhanger was agonising, but thankfully it's only a two month wait until the final instalment, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25565707.Tyrant__King___2_" title="Tyrant (King, #2) by T.M. Frazier" rel="nofollow noopener">Tyrant</a> hits my kindle. In the meantime, I know without a doubt I will not forget these fucking awesome characters.<br><br>This is part one of a duet, told in dual POV. Tyrant releases 17th August.<br><br><i>ARC gratefully received from the author in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br><a href="http://ilovebooklove-ab.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_969164963" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/969164963" />
    <a title="✰ Liz ✰ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27276528-liz"><img alt="✰ Liz ✰ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451097545p2/27276528.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/969164963?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✰ Liz ✰ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✰ Liz ✰ " href="/user/show/27276528-liz">✰ Liz ✰ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20611949-king">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=beautiful-cover">beautiful-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=my-heart-can-barely-take-it">my-heart-can-barely-take-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=love-this-author">love-this-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=high-steam-alert">high-steam-alert</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=action-packed">action-packed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=alpha-male-love">alpha-male-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=not-what-i-expected">not-what-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27276528-liz?shelf=high-angst-alert">high-angst-alert</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer969164963" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17669440516877837720"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434775496ra/15260801.gif' height='' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>" Things don’t always start out the way we want them to. It’s how they end that’s important.”</b><br/><br/>King is my third read by the dynamic T.M. Frazier. Her writing always leads to one thing…feelings. It seems, she has a gift at evoking the deepest and the darkest feelings out of her characters and therefore transferring their pains, joys, and triumphs deep into your own heart and soul.<br/><br/>Although there has been a great deal of buzz about the dark romance that exists in the story of King, I found a deeper </span>
  <span id="freeText17669440516877837720" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434775496ra/15260801.gif" height="" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>" Things don’t always start out the way we want them to. It’s how they end that’s important.”</b><br><br>King is my third read by the dynamic T.M. Frazier. Her writing always leads to one thing…feelings. It seems, she has a gift at evoking the deepest and the darkest feelings out of her characters and therefore transferring their pains, joys, and triumphs deep into your own heart and soul.<br><br>Although there has been a great deal of buzz about the dark romance that exists in the story of King, I found a deeper theme to be more prevalent in my appreciation for this story and that is friendship. Particularly, the friendship between two young boys that blooms into an unfaltering brotherhood.<br><br><b>The Friendship.....</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434917019i/15278159.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>“Name’s Samuel Clearwater. What’s yours?”-Preppy-</b><br><br>Preppy was a gangly nerd who was repeteadly abused and bullied by the people in his life. There was no safe place for him to exist. One day a burly bad boy named King stood up for his friend and protected him. The two formed a bond that would never be broken.<br><br><b>"Preppy and I. Two pees in a juvenile delinquent pod."</b><br><br>Preppy and King make plans to always be their to protect one another. They plan to do whatever it takes to take the world on. After successfully taking on the world, life seems to be perfect for these bad boys. Until, King is sent to prison to serve three years locked up.<br><br><b>King</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434917655i/15278182.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"Because when it comes to me and mine, I am the judge. I am the jury. And if need be, I am the motherf*cking executioner.”-King</b><br><br>Upon his release, King returns home to his tattoo parlor and his friends Preppy and Bear. And yet, he just can’t shake the filth that he has lived through. Women, alcohol, and even his love for tattooing can’t seem to fill the void that is eating away at his soul.<br><br><b>Doe</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434919775i/15278511.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>"I don’t know how old I am. I don’t know my real name.”-Doe</b><br><br>Doe a homeless "big-eyed" girl. Forgotten by her family, she is all alone. She is grappling to find her way. Starving to death, she finds a friend who offers her a way out. Desperate for food and shelter, she agrees to go with her new friend to a party where she can stake her claim on a biker. If she can find a man that will take her in, she can get her next meal and a safe place to be.<br><br>The party just so happens to be at King’s house. Doe meets King. Things do not progress has Doe had hoped. <br><br><b>“Who are you?”-King<br> “I’m no one,”-Doe</b><br><br>Due to choices of her “new friend”, Doe ends up somewhat of a prisoner to King. <br><br><b>"I didn’t know whether I wanted to kill her or f*ck her. Maybe both, but one thing was for sure. One way or another, I was going to make her scream. I was finally starting to feel like my old self again.-King"</b><br><br>What is remarkable about this read is the transformation that Doe makes as a heroine and the way that King aids her in making that change. The two begin the dance of attraction. King and Doe are a perfect dichotomy to the other. Hard versus soft. <br><br><b>"King was hard and scary as hell, so was his kiss. And if his words weren’t getting his point across, his kiss told me that he owned me. It made me forget for just a second that the man behind those lips was a raging psychopath.”-Doe</b><br><br>King becomes a shelter to Doe. Doe not only finds solace in King but she finds a friend in Preppy and Bear. As the layers of King begin to unravel, Doe begins to fall deeper in love with this man. Regardless of right or wrong, after time, King convinces Doe to let go of her fears and choose him.<br><br><b>"I loved sleeping with his big body next to me. I loved the way he made me feel so small. I loved the way his nostrils flared when he was about to kiss me, and then when he did, I loved that he kissed me like he was mad at me. Like it was my fault I was so desirable that he just had to put his lips to mine, his hands on me.”-Doe</b><br><br>In my humble opinion, towards the end of this read, King made some choices that were in direct contrast to his character regarding his feelings for Doe. He had labored long and hard to prove his feelings (including his worth and her worth) to Doe throughout the read. His behavior was somewhat jarring and truthfully, for me, unnerving. As the plot begins to unfold, I found these choices made me uncomfortable and truly heartbroken for Doe. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434920488i/15278602._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Regardless of the questions that these choices evoked regarding morality, the one remaining element is that King and Doe end up together. Does it matter that King made choices that I don’t like? No, not really. Did the writing cause me to pause and question my feelings on delicate subject matter? Yes! Therefore, Ms. Frazier was quite successful with her writing. Again, her bold choices have made me feel. We are not required to feel warm and fuzzy feelings in every book that we invest in. Instead, it is in these pieces of work colored with harshness and coldness, that we truly grow as a person and make decisions about what is truly black or white or just a little grey. I also feel it's imperative that I mention, I was not pleased with his decision at the end of the book either. Although I certainly understood his reasoning behind his choices, I prefer my heroes to be unwavering regarding their heroines. Perhaps, he will redeem himself for me in the next book?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434919775i/15278512.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, I highly recommend King to anyone who finds delight in darkness with a double dose of "rough anti-heroes". There are many endearing characters in this read. The writing is fluid and natural. T. M knows how to paint a vivid picture. However, a word of caution to my fellow readers who are sensitive to tricky subject matter. You will not have time to catch your breath. In fact, it will be hard to breathe at certain moments of this read. Additionally, there is, of course, a BIG cliffy and it is of course full of questions. In a way, I wish that I had waited to read this closer to the release of the next book. I wonder will King be able to redeem himself in my eyes? Will he and Doe find away through this jumbled web? If anyone can untangle this mess, I have faith that T.M. can. I, for one, will be waiting. <br><br><b>"Maybe, I did choose King being inside of me over breathing, because I couldn’t seem to catch my breath.”-Doe</b><br><br><b>BR with my girls War, Nawal and Loyda! Thank you ladies for a fantastic read!</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1434914663i/15277811.jpg" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17669440516877837720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sfJEVEzXQsAEEfis/RYClcHEp1Al1keLwwT7BETrJCT/+2I1tBSJIKZcmgZ+VhDg1mHNvzpUt0a5OPrZZ8NlbQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HerAhXA0pgq7fVMLbz/7WwqX3s2OhkF+wfH1xdng+LVT4+bkiPdt6hkwMaHsf+kuHTK0IpEEsbO7zfQY+si5/A==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15305620751703410793">T.M. (Tracey Marie) Frazier never dreamed that a single person would ever read a word she wrote when she published her first book. Now, she is a five-time USA Today bestselling author and her books have been translated into numerous languages and published all around the world. <br/><br/>T.M. enjoys writing what she calls ‘wrong side of the tracks romance’ with morally corrupt anti-heroes and ballsy heroine</span>
  <span id="freeText15305620751703410793" style="display:none">T.M. (Tracey Marie) Frazier never dreamed that a single person would ever read a word she wrote when she published her first book. Now, she is a five-time USA Today bestselling author and her books have been translated into numerous languages and published all around the world. <br /><br />T.M. enjoys writing what she calls ‘wrong side of the tracks romance’ with morally corrupt anti-heroes and ballsy heroines. <br /><br />Her books have been described as raw, dark and gritty. Basically, what that means, is while some authors are great at describing a flower as it blooms, T.M. is better at describing it in the final stages of decay. <br /><br />She loves meeting her readers, but if you see her at an event please don’t pinch her because she's not ready to wake up from this amazing dream. <br /><br />Join T.M. in Frazierland! <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/groups/tmfrazierland">www.facebook.com/groups/tmfrazierland</a></span>

    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
